Microsoft
(AZ-700)
Designing and Implementing Microsoft Azure Networking Solutions
388 Questions
Total:
Link: https://certyiq.com/papers/microsoft/az-700

Question: 1 CertyIQ
Your company has a single on-premises datacenter in Washington DC. The East US Azure region has a peering
location in Washington DC.
The company only has Azure resources in the East US region.
You need to implement ExpressRoute to support up to 1 Gbps. You must use only ExpressRoute Unlimited data
plans. The solution must minimize costs.
Which type of ExpressRoute circuits should you create?
A. ExpressRoute Local
B. ExpressRoute Direct
C. ExpressRoute Premium
D. ExpressRoute Standard
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A: ExpressRoute Local. Here's a detailed justification:
ExpressRoute Local is designed for connecting to Azure regions within the same metro area where your on-
premises infrastructure resides. In this scenario, the East US region has a peering location in Washington DC,
which is also where the company's on-premises datacenter is located. Therefore, ExpressRoute Local
perfectly fits the geographical requirements.
ExpressRoute Local offers a lower cost compared to ExpressRoute Standard or Premium, as it's optimized for
connectivity within the same metro area. The question emphasizes minimizing costs, making ExpressRoute
Local the preferred option if it meets the technical requirements.
The requirement of 1 Gbps bandwidth is also satisfied by ExpressRoute Local, as it supports various
bandwidth options, including 1 Gbps. Using an Unlimited data plan is also supported by the ExpressRoute
Local Circuit.
ExpressRoute Standard provides access to all Azure regions within a geographical zone, which is not
necessary in this case as the company only uses the East US region. ExpressRoute Premium extends this
further, providing global access, even more unnecessary features for the given requirements. ExpressRoute
Direct involves a dedicated connection to Microsoft's network, intended for very high bandwidth requirements
(40 Gbps or 100 Gbps) and isn't suitable for a 1 Gbps requirement. Therefore, standard, premium and direct are
unnecessarily expensive.
In summary, ExpressRoute Local efficiently addresses the company's needs for connecting to the East US
region from Washington DC, supporting the required bandwidth and offering a cost-effective solution
compared to other ExpressRoute options while satisfying the 'Unlimited data plan' constraint.
Relevant documentation:
ExpressRoute Local: https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/expressroute/expressroute-faqs (Look for
information on local peering.)
ExpressRoute Connectivity Models: https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/expressroute/expressroute-
connectivity-models
ExpressRoute Pricing: https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/pricing/details/expressroute/ (Compare costs
between Local, Standard, and Premium.)
Question: 2 CertyIQ

You are planning an Azure Point-to-Site (P2S) VPN that will use OpenVPN.
Users will authenticate by an on-premises Active Directory domain.
Which additional service should you deploy to support the VPN authentication?
A. an Azure key vault
B. a RADIUS server
C. a certification authority
D. Azure Active Directory (Azure AD) Application Proxy
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B. a RADIUS server. Here's why:
OpenVPN connections, especially when integrated with on-premises Active Directory for authentication, often
rely on the RADIUS (Remote Authentication Dial-In User Service) protocol. RADIUS acts as a central
authentication and authorization system. When a user attempts to connect via OpenVPN, their credentials are
sent to the Azure VPN gateway. The VPN gateway then forwards these credentials to the RADIUS server.
The RADIUS server, integrated with Active Directory, verifies the user's credentials against the on-premises
domain. Upon successful validation, the RADIUS server sends an approval message back to the VPN gateway,
allowing the user to establish the VPN connection. Without a RADIUS server, the VPN gateway would not be
able to properly authenticate users against the on-premises Active Directory.
Azure Key Vault (A) is used for managing secrets and certificates, not for direct user authentication in this
scenario. A certification authority (C) issues digital certificates, primarily used for certificate-based
authentication, which isn't the specified method. Azure Active Directory Application Proxy (D) allows on-
premises web applications to be accessed remotely, but it doesn't facilitate authentication for VPN
connections directly against on-premises Active Directory using OpenVPN. While Azure AD can be used for
VPN authentication, the scenario specifically mentions authentication against an on-premises AD domain. A
RADIUS server bridges the gap, enabling authentication against the on-premises AD through the VPN.
Further research:
Azure VPN Gateway P2S with RADIUS: https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/vpn-gateway/vpn-gateway-
howto-radius-ps
RADIUS protocol: https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RADIUS
Question: 3 CertyIQ
You plan to configure BGP for a Site-to-Site VPN connection between a datacenter and Azure.
Which two Azure resources should you configure? Each correct answer presents a part of the solution. (Choose
two.)
NOTE: Each correct selection is worth one point.
A. a virtual network gateway
B. Azure Application Gateway
C. Azure Firewall
D. a local network gateway
E. Azure Front Door

Answer: AD
Explanation:
The correct answer is A and D. Let's break down why:
1. A. Virtual Network Gateway: A virtual network gateway is a crucial component when establishing a
Site-to-Site VPN connection from your on-premises network to Azure. It serves as the VPN endpoint
in Azure. BGP (Border Gateway Protocol) dynamically exchanges routing information between your
on-premises network and the Azure virtual network through this gateway. You need to enable BGP on
the virtual network gateway to facilitate this dynamic routing.
2. D. Local Network Gateway: A local network gateway represents your on-premises VPN device in
Azure. It contains information about the on-premises VPN device's IP address, address prefixes that
are routable on the on-premises network, and the BGP ASN (Autonomous System Number) of the on-
premises network. When BGP is configured, Azure needs to know the ASN of your on-premises
network to establish the BGP peering relationship. It allows Azure to send routes learned from the
virtual network to the on-premises network, and vice-versa.
Why the other options are incorrect:
1. B. Azure Application Gateway: An Application Gateway is a web traffic load balancer that manages
traffic to web applications. It has no direct role in establishing or configuring Site-to-Site VPNs or
BGP.
2. C. Azure Firewall: Azure Firewall is a managed, cloud-based network security service that protects
your Azure virtual network resources. While it can be used in conjunction with a VPN connection, it's
not directly involved in the BGP configuration process for the Site-to-Site VPN.
3. E. Azure Front Door: Azure Front Door is a global, scalable entry point that uses the Microsoft global
network to create fast, secure, and widely scalable web applications. Like Application Gateway, it
operates at a different layer (application layer) and is not involved in the IP-level routing required for
VPN and BGP.
In summary: To establish a Site-to-Site VPN connection with BGP between your datacenter and Azure, you
must configure a Virtual Network Gateway to act as the Azure VPN endpoint and a Local Network Gateway to
represent your on-premises network and VPN device in Azure, including its ASN. These two resources work
together to enable dynamic route exchange between your on-premises network and Azure using BGP.
Authoritative Links:
1. About VPN Gateway: Configure BGP
2. Configure BGP on Azure VPN Gateway
3. Create a Site-to-Site connection using the Resource Manager with BGP
Question: 4 CertyIQ
You fail to establish a Site-to-Site VPN connection between your company's main office and an Azure virtual
network.
You need to troubleshoot what prevents you from establishing the IPsec tunnel.
Which diagnostic log should you review?
A. IKEDiagnosticLog
B. RouteDiagnosticLog
C. GatewayDiagnosticLog
D. TunnelDiagnosticLog

Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A. IKEDiagnosticLog.
Establishing a Site-to-Site VPN connection relies heavily on the Internet Key Exchange (IKE) protocol. IKE is
responsible for setting up the security association (SA) between the VPN gateways, which includes
authentication, encryption, and key exchange. If the IPsec tunnel cannot be established, the initial IKE
negotiation is the most likely culprit.
The IKEDiagnosticLog specifically captures detailed information regarding the IKE negotiation process. This
log contains events such as IKE version negotiation, authentication failures, encryption/hashing algorithm
mismatches, Diffie-Hellman key exchange errors, and SA establishment attempts. By examining these logs,
you can pinpoint exactly where the IKE negotiation failed, which is crucial for identifying configuration errors,
compatibility issues, or authentication problems between the on-premises VPN device and the Azure VPN
gateway.
Option B, RouteDiagnosticLog, focuses on routing-related information, such as route table configurations and
route propagation. While routing is important for traffic flow after the IPsec tunnel is established, it is not
directly involved in the initial tunnel establishment.
Option C, GatewayDiagnosticLog, is a more general log that provides overall health and status information
about the Azure VPN gateway. While useful for monitoring the gateway, it lacks the granularity needed to
diagnose specific IKE negotiation failures.
Option D, TunnelDiagnosticLog, would be useful after the tunnel is established to diagnose issues with data
flowing through the tunnel, but it is not directly related to the initial IPsec connection establishment failure.
Therefore, for troubleshooting the inability to establish an IPsec tunnel, the IKEDiagnosticLog provides the
most specific and relevant diagnostic information to pinpoint the root cause of the problem.
Further Reading:
Azure VPN Gateway Diagnostics: https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/vpn-gateway/vpn-gateway-
troubleshoot-vpn-connection
About VPN devices and IPsec/IKE parameters for Site-to-Site VPN Gateway connections:
https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/vpn-gateway/vpn-gateway-about-vpn-devices
Question: 5 CertyIQ
You have an Azure virtual network and an on-premises datacenter.
You are planning a Site-to-Site VPN connection between the datacenter and the virtual network.
Which two resources should you include in your plan? Each correct answer presents part of the solution.
NOTE: Each correct selection is worth one point.
A. a user-defined route
B. a virtual network gateway
C. Azure Firewall
D. Azure Web Application Firewall (WAF)
E. an on-premises data gateway
F. an Azure application gateway
G. a local network gateway

Answer: BG
Explanation:
The correct answer is B. a virtual network gateway and G. a local network gateway.
To establish a Site-to-Site VPN connection between an Azure virtual network and an on-premises datacenter,
specific resources are essential on both ends of the connection.
A virtual network gateway is a crucial component within Azure. It provides the VPN endpoint for the Azure
virtual network and enables secure connectivity with the on-premises environment. This gateway creates an
encrypted tunnel through which data can flow between the Azure virtual network and the on-premises
network. Without it, there's no entry point for the VPN connection within Azure.
A local network gateway represents the on-premises VPN device or network within Azure. It contains
information about the on-premises VPN device, such as its public IP address and the address prefixes of the
on-premises network. Azure uses this information to route traffic correctly and establish a secure connection.
Think of it as Azure's understanding of your on-premises network and how to reach it.
Option A (a user-defined route) is not directly required for the initial Site-to-Site VPN setup, but can be used
to influence how traffic is routed within Azure. Option C (Azure Firewall) provides network security but is not
essential for establishing the VPN connection. Option D (Azure Web Application Firewall) protects web
applications and not relevant for this scenario. Option E (on-premises data gateway) is for connecting to on-
premises data sources from Azure services like Logic Apps, not for Site-to-Site VPN. Option F (Azure
application gateway) is for managing and routing web traffic, not establishing VPN connections.
Therefore, the Virtual Network Gateway and Local Network Gateway are mandatory for setting up a Site-to-
Site VPN between Azure and on-premises network.
References:
About VPN Gateway
Create a Site-to-Site VPN connection in the Azure portal

support failing over to a Site-to-Site VPN connection if there is an ExpressRoute failure.
What should you configure? To answer, select the appropriate options in the answer area.

Hot Area:

ExpressRoute virtual network gateway. The ExpressRoute virtual network gateway enables the VNet to
connect to the ExpressRoute circuit used for connectivity with your on-premises network.
VPN virtual network gateway. The VPN virtual network gateway enables the VNet to connect to the VPN
appliance in the on-premises network. The VPN virtual network gateway is configured to accept requests
from the on-premises network only through the VPN appliance

Question: 7 CertyIQ
Your company has an on-premises network and three Azure subscriptions named Subscription1, Subscription2, and
Subscription3.
The departments at the company use the Azure subscriptions as shown in the following table.
All the resources in the subscriptions are in either the West US Azure region or the West US 2 Azure region.
You plan to connect all the subscriptions to the on-premises network by using ExpressRoute.
What is the minimum number of ExpressRoute circuits required?
A. 1
B. 2
C. 3
D. 4
E. 5
Answer: A
Explanation:
1
Managing Authorization
The circuit owner can share a circuit with up to 10 Azure subscriptions. The circuit owner can view who has
been authorized to the circuit. The owner can revoke the authorization at any time.
https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/enable-multiple-subscription-

Question: 8 CertyIQ
Your company has offices in New York and Amsterdam. The company has an Azure subscription. Both offices
connect to Azure by using a Site-to-Site VPN connection.
The office in Amsterdam uses resources in the North Europe Azure region. The office in New York uses resources
in the East US Azure region.
You need to implement ExpressRoute circuits to connect each office to the nearest Azure region. Once the
ExpressRoute circuits are connected, the on-premises computers in the Amsterdam office must be able to connect
to the on-premises servers in the New York office by using the ExpressRoute circuits.
Which ExpressRoute option should you use?

A. ExpressRoute FastPath
B. ExpressRoute Global Reach
C. ExpressRoute Direct
D. ExpressRoute Local
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B. ExpressRoute Global Reach. Here's a detailed justification:
ExpressRoute Global Reach is specifically designed to enable private connectivity between your on-premises
networks that are connected to different ExpressRoute circuits. In this scenario, the Amsterdam office
connects to Azure via ExpressRoute in North Europe, and the New York office connects via ExpressRoute in
East US. The requirement is that on-premises networks in Amsterdam need to communicate with on-premises
networks in New York using ExpressRoute.
ExpressRoute Global Reach addresses this directly by allowing you to create a bridge between your
ExpressRoute circuits, allowing data to flow directly between your on-premises locations without traversing
the public internet or routing through Azure virtual networks. This ensures a private and potentially lower-
latency connection than traversing the public internet or going through Azure virtual networks.
Why other options are incorrect:
ExpressRoute FastPath: Improves data path performance by sending network traffic directly to virtual
machines in a virtual network, bypassing the Azure gateway. It's primarily concerned with improving
connectivity within an Azure virtual network, not between on-premises networks. While FastPath improves VM
to on-premises communication after traffic reaches the virtual network, it doesn't solve the problem of
connecting the two different on-premises networks via ExpressRoute.
ExpressRoute Direct: Allows you to connect directly to Microsoft's global network at peering locations. It's
used for large bandwidth requirements and requires significant investment in infrastructure. It doesn't
inherently provide the bridging functionality between two distinct ExpressRoute circuits required here. It
allows a direct connection for data that normally goes through the service provider, but it does not necessarily
provide a path to connect two separate ExpressRoute circuits.
ExpressRoute Local: Is designed to optimize connectivity to Azure resources within a specific region, usually
the region where the ExpressRoute circuit is located. It reduces data transfer costs by avoiding data egress
charges to other regions. However, it does not provide a means to connect on-premises networks connected
to separate ExpressRoute circuits across different regions.
In conclusion, ExpressRoute Global Reach provides the essential functionality of connecting on-premises
networks connected to different ExpressRoute circuits, enabling communication between Amsterdam and
New York in a private and efficient manner.
Supporting Links:
ExpressRoute Global Reach
ExpressRoute FastPath
ExpressRoute Direct
ExpressRoute Local
Question: 9 CertyIQ
HOTSPOT -
You have an Azure subscription that contains a single virtual network and a virtual network gateway.

You need to ensure that administrators can use Point-to-Site (P2S) VPN connections to access resources in the
virtual network. The connections must be authenticated by Azure Active Directory (Azure AD).
What should you configure? To answer, select the appropriate options in the answer area.
NOTE: Each correct selection is worth one point.
Hot Area:
Answer:
Explanation:
Box 1: An enterprise application
Enable Azure AD authentication on the VPN gateway:
1. Locate the Directory ID of the directory that you want to use for authentication. It's listed in the properties
section of the Active Directory page.
2. Under your Azure AD, in Enterprise applications, you see Azure VPN listed.
Copy the Directory ID.
3. Sign in to the Azure portal as a user that is assigned the Global administrator role.
4. Next, give admin consent. Copy and paste the URL that pertains to your deployment location in the address
bar of your browser.

5. Select the Global Admin account if prompted.
6. Select Accept when prompted.
7. Under your Azure AD, in Enterprise applications, you see Azure VPN listed.

Box 2: Open VPN (SSL)
When you connect to your VNet using Point-to-Site, you have a choice of which protocol to use. The protocol
you use determines the authentication options that are available to you. If you want to use Azure Active
Directory authentication, you can do so when using the OpenVPN protocol.
Reference:
https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/vpn-gateway/openvpn-azure-ad-tenant
Question: 10 CertyIQ
HOTSPOT -
You have the hybrid network shown in the Network Diagram exhibit.
You have a peering connection between Vnet1 and Vnet2 as shown in the Peering-Vnet1-Vnet2 exhibit.

You have a peering connection between Vnet1 and Vnet3 as shown in the Peering-Vnet1-Vnet3 exhibit.

For each of the following statements, select Yes if the statement is true. Otherwise, select No.
NOTE: Each correct selection is worth one point.
Hot Area:
Answer:
Explanation:
Box 1: Yes -
Virtual network peering seamlessly connects two Azure virtual networks, merging the two virtual networks
into one for connectivity purposes.
Box 2: No -
No Virtual Gateway is used.
Gateway transit is a peering property that lets one virtual network use the VPN gateway in the peered virtual
network for cross-premises or VNet-to-VNet connectivity. The following diagram shows how gateway transit
works with virtual network peering.

In the diagram, gateway transit allows the peered virtual networks to use the Azure VPN gateway in Hub-RM.
Connectivity available on the VPN gateway, including S2S, P2S, and VNet-to-VNet connections, applies to all
three virtual networks.
Box 3: No -
No Virtual Gateway is used.
Reference:
https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/vpn-gateway/vpn-gateway-peering-gateway-transit
Question: 11 CertyIQ
HOTSPOT -
You have the Azure environment shown in the exhibit.
You have virtual network peering between Vnet1 and Vnet2. You have virtual network peering between Vnet4 and
Vnet5. The virtual network peering is configured as shown in the following table.

For each of the following statements, select Yes if the statement is true. Otherwise, select No.
Hot Area:
Answer:
Explanation:
Box 1: Yes -
Virtual network peering seamlessly connects two Azure virtual networks, merging the two virtual networks
into one for connectivity purposes. Gateway transit is a peering property that lets one virtual network use the
VPN gateway in the peered virtual network for cross-premises or VNet-to-VNet connectivity.
The following diagram shows how gateway transit works with virtual network peering.

In the diagram, gateway transit allows the peered virtual networks to use the Azure VPN gateway in Hub-RM.
Connectivity available on the VPN gateway, including S2S, P2S, and VNet-to-VNet connections, applies to all
three virtual networks.
In hub-and-spoke network architecture, gateway transit allows spoke virtual networks to share the VPN
gateway in the hub, instead of deploying VPN gateways in every spoke virtual network.
Box 2: Yes -
VM2 uses the remote gateway GW1 to reach VM4.
Box 3: yes
Select Block all traffic to the remote virtual network if you don't want traffic to flow to the peered virtual
network by default. You can select this setting if you have peering between two virtual networks but
occasionally want to disable default traffic flow between the two. You may find enabling/disabling is more
convenient than deleting and re-creating peerings. When this setting is selected, traffic doesn't flow between
the peered virtual networks by default; however, traffic may still flow if explicitly allowed through a network
security group rule that includes the appropriate IP addresses or application security groups.

Question: 13 CertyIQ
You have an Azure virtual network named Vnet1 and an on-premises network. The on-premises network has policy-
based VPN devices.
In Vnet1, you deploy a virtual network gateway named GW1 that uses a SKU of VpnGw1 and is route-based.
You have a Site-to-Site VPN connection for GW1 as shown in the following exhibit.
You need to ensure that the on-premises network can connect to the route-based GW1.
What should you do before you create the connection?
A. Set Connection Mode to ResponderOnly.
B. Set BGP to Enabled.
C. Set Use Azure Private IP Address to Enabled.
D. Set IPsec / IKE policy to Custom.

Answer: D
Explanation:
Previously, when working with policy-based VPNs, you were limited to using the policy-based VPN gateway
Basic SKU and could only connect to 1 on-premises VPN/firewall device. Now, using custom IPsec/IKE policy,
you can use a route-based VPN gateway and connect to multiple policy-based VPN/firewall devices. To make
a policy-based VPN connection using a route-based VPN gateway, configure the route-based VPN gateway to
use prefix-based traffic selectors with the option "PolicyBasedTrafficSelectors". as per
Reference:
https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/vpn-gateway/vpn-gateway-connect-multiple-policybased
Question: 14 CertyIQ
HOTSPOT
-
Your on-premises network contains a VPN device.
You have an Azure subscription that contains a virtual network and a virtual network gateway.
You need to create a Site-to-Site VPN connection that has a custom cryptographic policy.
How should you complete the PowerShell script? To answer, select the appropriate options in the answer area.
NOTE: Each correct selection is worth one point.
Answer:
Explanation:
1. New-AzIpsecPolicy .

This cmdlet is used to create an IPsec policy for a virtual network gateway connection in Azure.
The policy defines encryption algorithms, integrity algorithms, Diffie-Hellman (DH) groups, and SA (Security
Association) lifetimes.
The parameters used:
-IkeEncryption AES256: Uses AES 256-bit encryption for IKE (Internet Key Exchange).
-IkeIntegrity SHA384: Uses SHA-384 for integrity.
-DhGroup DHGroup24: Specifies Diffie-Hellman group 24 for key exchange.
-IpsecEncryption AES256: Uses AES-256 encryption for IPsec.
-IpsecIntegrity SHA256: Uses SHA-256 for integrity.
-PfsGroup PFSGroup14: Specifies Perfect Forward Secrecy (PFS) group 14.
-SALifeTimeSeconds 14400: Defines the lifetime of a security association in seconds.
-SADataSizeKilobytes 102400000: Specifies the maximum data size before a rekeying event.
2. New-AzVirtualNetworkGatewayConnection.
This cmdlet is used to create a connection between a virtual network gateway and another network (such as
an on-premises VPN device).
The parameters used:
-Name $Connection6: Specifies the name of the connection.
-ResourceGroupName $RG1: Defines the resource group in which the connection is deployed.
-VirtualNetworkGateway1 $vnetgw: Specifies the virtual network gateway object.
-LocalNetworkGateway2 $lng6: Specifies the local network gateway object.
-Location $location: Defines the location of the resource.
-ConnectionType IPsec: Specifies the connection type as IPsec VPN.
-IpsecPolicies $policy: Assigns the previously created IPsec policy to the connection.
-SharedKey 'AzureABC123': Defines the shared key for authentication.
Question: 15 CertyIQ
HOTSPOT
-
You have an Azure virtual network and an on-premises datacenter that connect by using a Site-to-Site VPN tunnel.
You need to ensure that all traffic from the virtual network to the internet is routed through the datacenter.
How should you complete the PowerShell script to configure forced tunneling? To answer, select the appropriate
options in the answer area.
NOTE: Each correct selection is worth one point.

Answer:
Explanation:
1. Get-AzLocalNetworkGateway
This cmdlet is used to retrieve an existing local network gateway in Azure.
A local network gateway represents an on-premises VPN device or a remote VPN gateway in a site-to-site
VPN setup.
The retrieved object is stored in the variable $force1, which will be used later in the script.
Usage in the Script:
powershell
Copy
Edit
$force1 = Get-AzLocalNetworkGateway -Name "HQ" -ResourceGroupName "ForcedTunneling"
Retrieves the local network gateway named "HQ" from the resource group "ForcedTunneling".

2. Set-AzVirtualNetworkGatewayDefaultSite.
This cmdlet is used to configure forced tunneling by setting a default site for a virtual network gateway.
Forced tunneling ensures that all internet-bound traffic from Azure virtual machines is routed through an on-
premises network instead of going directly to the internet.
The default site is usually an on-premises VPN device (represented by a local network gateway).
Usage in the Script:
powershell
Copy
Edit
Set-AzVirtualNetworkGatewayDefaultSite -VirtualNetworkGateway $force2 -DefaultSite $force1
$force2 represents the Azure Virtual Network Gateway retrieved earlier.
$force1 represents the Local Network Gateway retrieved in the first step.
This command sets the on-premises site as the default route, ensuring that all internet traffic is tunneled
through the local network gateway.
Question: 16 CertyIQ
You are planning an Azure deployment that will contain three virtual networks in the East US Azure region as
shown in the following table.
A Site-to-Site VPN will connect Vnet1 to your company’s on-premises network.
You need to recommend a solution that ensures that the virtual machines on all the virtual networks can
communicate with the on-premises network. The solution must minimize costs.
What should you recommend for Vnet2 and Vnet3?
A.VNet-to-VNet VPN connections
B.peering
C.service endpoints
D.route tables
Answer: B
Explanation:
B. Peering
A Site-to-Site (S2S) VPN connects VNet1 to your on-premises network. To ensure that virtual machines in
VNet2 and VNet3 can also communicate with the on-premises network while minimizing costs, VNet Peering
is the best solution.

Question: 17 CertyIQ
Your company has an office in New York.
The company has an Azure subscription that contains the virtual networks shown in the following table.
You need to connect the virtual networks to the office by using ExpressRoute. The solution must meet the
following requirements:
• The connection must have up to 1 Gbps of bandwidth.
• The office must have access to all the virtual networks.
• Costs must be minimized.
How many ExpressRoute circuits should be provisioned, and which ExpressRoute SKU should you enable?
A. one ExpressRoute Premium circuit
B. two ExpressRoute Premium circuits
C. four ExpressRoute Standard circuits
D. one ExpressRoute Standard circuit
Answer: A
Explanation:
one ExpressRoute Premium circuit
Key Requirements:
Connect the office in New York to multiple Azure virtual networks.
Bandwidth requirement: up to 1 Gbps.
Minimize costs while providing access to all virtual networks.
Why the Answer is "One ExpressRoute Premium Circuit":
ExpressRoute Premium allows global connectivity, enabling a single circuit to connect to multiple virtual
networks across different Azure regions.
The table likely lists virtual networks across multiple regions, so the Premium SKU is required for this global
connectivity.
With Premium, you can use one circuit to connect to all virtual networks, avoiding the cost of provisioning
separate circuits for each virtual network or region.
1 Gbps Bandwidth: A single ExpressRoute circuit supports up to 1 Gbps, meeting the requirement.
Why Other Options Are Incorrect:
B. Two ExpressRoute Premium Circuits:

This doubles the cost unnecessarily. One Premium circuit is sufficient to connect the office to all virtual
networks.
C. Four ExpressRoute Standard Circuits:
ExpressRoute Standard only supports connectivity within the same geopolitical region (e.g., East US, West
US). If the virtual networks are in different regions, this would require multiple circuits and higher costs.
Also, provisioning 4 separate circuits is inefficient and expensive.
D. One ExpressRoute Standard Circuit:
The Standard SKU only supports virtual network connections within the same region or geopolitical zone.
If the virtual networks span multiple regions, the Standard SKU cannot provide connectivity to all of them.
Key Points About ExpressRoute SKUs:
ExpressRoute Standard:
Connectivity within a single Azure region or geopolitical zone (e.g., East US, West US).
Lower cost but limited to regional connections.
ExpressRoute Premium:
Provides global connectivity across multiple regions.
Necessary for scenarios where you need to connect to virtual networks in multiple Azure regions.
Cost Minimization:
By using a single ExpressRoute Premium circuit, the company minimizes costs while meeting the
requirements for bandwidth and global access.

Question: 19 CertyIQ
You have an Azure subscription that contains the resources shown in the following table.
You create a virtual network named Vnet2 in the West US region.
You plan to enable peering between Vnet1 and Vnet2.
You need to ensure that the virtual machines connected to Vnet2 can connect to VM1 and VM2 via LB1.
What should you do?
A. From the Peerings settings of Vnet2, set Traffic forwarded from remote virtual network to Allow.
B. Change the Floating IP configurations of LB1.
C. From the Peerings settings of Vnet1, set Traffic forwarded from remote virtual network to Allow.
D. Change the SKU of LB1.
Answer: D
Explanation:
D. Change the SKU of LB1.
When enabling peering between VNet1 and VNet2, and ensuring that virtual machines connected to VNet2
can connect to VM1 and VM2 via Load Balancer (LB1), the key factor is the Load Balancer SKU. Standard Load
Balancer SKU supports cross-region and VNet peering, whereas the Basic Load Balancer SKU does not.
To ensure connectivity across peered VNets through a load balancer, you need to use the Standard SKU.
Changing the SKU of LB1 to Standard will enable the virtual machines in VNet2 to connect to VM1 and VM2 via
LB1, meeting the requirement.
Question: 20 CertyIQ
DRAG DROP
-
Your on-premises network contains an Active Directory Domain Services (AD DS) domain named contoso.com that
has an internal certification authority (CA).
You have an Azure subscription.
You deploy an Azure application gateway named AppGwy1 and perform the following actions:
• Configure an HTTP listener
• Associate a routing rule with the listener
You need to configure AppGwy1 to perform mutual authentication for requests from domain-joined computers to
contoso.com.
Which four actions should you perform in sequence? To answer, move the appropriate actions from the list of

actions to the answer area and arrange them in the correct order.
Answer:
Explanation:
From AppGw1, create an SSL profile.
The SSL profile defines SSL policies, including allowed TLS versions and cipher suites.
From an on-premises computer, upload a certificate to AppGw1.
The SSL certificate (PFX format) is required for secure communication.
It is uploaded and associated with the Application Gateway.
From AppGw1, add an HTTP listener and associate the listener to the SSL profile.
The listener is configured to accept HTTPS requests and is linked to the SSL profile.
From AppGw1, create a routing rule.
The rule maps the listener to a backend pool and specifies how traffic should be handled.

HOTSPOT
-
You have an on-premises datacenter.
You have an Azure subscription that contains 10 virtual machines and a virtual network named VNet1 in the East US

You need to connect the datacenter to VNet1 by using ExpressRoute. The solution must meet the following
requirements:
•Maintain connectivity to the virtual machines if two availability zones fail.
•Support 1000-Mbps connections.
•Minimize costs.
What should you include in the solution? To answer, select the appropriate options in the answer area.
NOTE: Each correct selection is worth one point.
Answer:
Explanation:

One ExpressRoute Standard circuit.
An ExpressRoute circuit is a dedicated network connection to Azure.
Standard circuits allow access to Azure services across global Microsoft regions.
Only one ExpressRoute circuit is needed for a basic setup.

Question: 26 CertyIQ

Case Study -
This is a case study. Case studies are not timed separately. You can use as much exam time as you would like to
complete each case. However, there may be additional case studies and sections on this exam. You must manage
your time to ensure that you are able to complete all questions included on this exam in the time provided.
To answer the questions included in a case study, you will need to reference information that is provided in the
case study. Case studies might contain exhibits and other resources that provide more information about the
scenario that is described in the case study. Each question is independent of the other questions in this case study.
At the end of this case study, a review screen will appear. This screen allows you to review your answers and to
make changes before you move to the next section of the exam. After you begin a new section, you cannot return
to this section.
To start the case study -
To display the first question in this case study, click the Next button. Use the buttons in the left pane to explore
the content of the case study before you answer the questions. Clicking these buttons displays information such
as business requirements, existing environment, and problem statements. When you are ready to answer a
question, click the Question button to return to the question.
Overview -
Litware, Inc. is a financial company that has a main datacenter in Boston and 20 branch offices across the United
States. Users have Android, iOS, and Windows 10 devices.
Existing Environment -
Hybrid Environment -
The on-premises network contains an Active Directory forest named litwareinc.com that syncs to an Azure Active
Directory (Azure AD) tenant named litwareinc.com by using Azure AD Connect.
All offices connect to a virtual network named Vnet1 by using a Site-to-Site VPN connection.
Azure Environment -
Litware has an Azure subscription named Sub1 that is linked to the litwareinc.com Azure AD tenant. Sub1 contains
resources in the East US Azure region as shown in the following table.
A diagram of the resource in the East US Azure region is shown in the Azure Network Diagram exhibit.
There is bidirectional peering between Vnet1 and Vnet2. There is bidirectional peering between Vnet1 and Vnet3.
Currently, Vnet2 and Vnet3 cannot communicate directly.
Azure Network Diagram -

Requirements -
Business Requirements -
Litware wants to minimize costs whenever possible, as long as all other requirements are met.
Virtual Networking Requirements -
Litware identifies the following virtual networking requirements:
•Direct the default route of 0.0.0.0/0 on Vnet2 and Vnet3 to the Boston datacenter over an ExpressRoute circuit.
•Ensure that the records in the cloud.litwareinc.com can be resolved from the on-premises locations.
•Automatically register the DNS names of Azure virtual machines to the cloud.litwareinc.com zone.
•Minimize the size of the subnets allocated to platform-managed services.
•Allow traffic from VMScaleSet1 to VMScaleSet2 on the TCP port 443 only.
Hybrid Networking Requirements -
Litware identifies the following hybrid networking requirements:
•Users must be able to connect to Vnet1 by using a Point-to-Site (P2S) VPN when working remotely. Connections
must be authenticated by Azure AD.
•Latency of the traffic between the Boston datacenter and all the virtual networks must be minimized.
•The Boston datacenter must connect to the Azure virtual networks by using an ExpressRoute FastPath
connection.
•Traffic between Vnet2 and Vnet3 must be routed through Vnet1.
PaaS Networking Requirements -
Litware identifies the following networking requirements for platform as a service (PaaS):
•The storage1 account must be accessible from all on-premises locations without exposing the public endpoint of

storage1.
•The storage2 account must be accessible from Vnet2 and Vnet3 without exposing the public endpoint of
storage2.
You need to connect Vnet2 and Vnet3. The solution must meet the virtual networking requirements and the
business requirements.
Which two actions should you include in the solution? Each correct answer presents part of the solution.
NOTE: Each correct selection is worth one point.
A.On the peering from Vnet1, select Allow for Traffic forwarded from remote virtual network.
B.On the peerings from Vnet2 and Vnet3, select Allow for Traffic forwarded from remote virtual network.
C.On the peering from Vnet1, select Use the remote virtual network's gateway or Route Server.
D.On the peering from Vnet1, select Allow for Traffic to remote virtual network.
E.On the peerings from Vnet2 and Vnet3, select Use the remote virtual network's gateway or Route Server.
Answer: BE
Explanation:
B : On the peerings from Vnet2 and Vnet3, select Allow for Traffic forwarded from remote virtual network and
E: On the peerings from Vnet2 and Vnet3, select Use the remote virtual network's gateway or Route Server.
Allow for Traffic Forwarded from Remote Virtual Network:
By selecting this option on the peerings from Vnet2 and Vnet3, you allow traffic that comes from other virtual
networks to be forwarded to Vnet2 and Vnet3. This is essential for enabling the traffic to flow between the
virtual networks.
Use the Remote Virtual Network's Gateway or Route Server:
By selecting this option on the peerings from Vnet2 and Vnet3, you allow these virtual networks to use the
gateway (VPN or ExpressRoute) in another virtual network (Vnet1) for connectivity. This is important when you
have a central gateway (like in a hub-and-spoke topology) and want the spoke virtual networks (Vnet2 and
Vnet3) to use the hub's gateway for connectivity.

Question: 29 CertyIQ
You have three on-premises networks.
You have an Azure subscription that contains a Basic Azure virtual WAN. The virtual WAN contains a single virtual
hub and a virtual network gateway that is limited to a throughput of 1 Gbps.
The on-premises networks connect to the virtual WAN by using Site-to-Site (S2S) VPN connections.
You need to increase the throughput of the virtual WAN to 3 Gbps. The solution must minimize administrative
effort.
What should you do?
A.Upgrade the virtual WAN to the Standard SKU.
B.Add an additional VPN gateway to the Azure subscription.
C.Create an additional virtual hub.
D.Increase the number of gateway scale units.
Answer: D

Explanation:
The correct answer is D. Increase the number of gateway scale units.
Here's a detailed justification:
A Basic Azure Virtual WAN is limited in functionality and throughput, including the VPN gateway
performance. While upgrading to a Standard SKU (Option A) unlocks more features and higher scalability
limits, it doesn't directly increase the gateway throughput. It's a prerequisite for increasing the gateway scale
units, but not the immediate solution.
Adding another VPN gateway to the subscription (Option B) won't increase the single virtual WAN gateway's
throughput. The aim is to enhance the existing connection's capacity, not to introduce another one managed
separately, especially since you are only using one virtual hub.
Creating an additional virtual hub (Option C) introduces unnecessary complexity. Virtual hubs are designed for
larger, more segmented networks where different routing domains are desired. Creating another virtual hub
would require re-architecting the existing connections and potentially additional costs.
Increasing the number of gateway scale units (Option D) directly addresses the throughput limitation. Azure
VPN gateway scale units determine the aggregate bandwidth available for all connections terminating at that
gateway. By increasing the scale units, you're effectively allocating more resources to the VPN gateway,
enabling it to handle a higher throughput (up to 3 Gbps in this case). This approach leverages the existing
infrastructure and provides a scalable solution for increasing network performance with minimal disruption.
You must have a Standard SKU Virtual WAN to increase the gateway scale units. Since the question only asks
what the immediate next step is, Option D is the correct answer.
References:
About VPN Gateway settings - Azure VPN Gateway | Microsoft Learn
Virtual WAN SKUs - Azure Virtual WAN | Microsoft Learn
Plan your VPN gateway SKU changes - Azure VPN Gateway | Microsoft Learn
Question: 30 CertyIQ
You have 10 on-premises networks that are connected by using a 3rd party Software Defined Wide Area Network
(SD-WAN) solution. You have an Azure subscription that contains five virtual networks.
You plan to connect the Azure virtual networks and the on-premises networks by using an Azure Virtual WAN with
a single virtual WAN hub.
You need to ensure that the Azure Virtual WAN can act as a node in the 3rd party SD-WAN solution.
What should you include in the solution?
A.An Azure Virtual WAN ExpressRoute gateway
B.A Network Virtual Appliance (NVA)
C.A Site to site gateway (VPN gateway)
D.A Point to site gateway (User VPN gateway)
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B. A Network Virtual Appliance (NVA).
Here's why:

The key requirement is integrating Azure Virtual WAN with a 3rd party SD-WAN solution, effectively making
Azure a node within that SD-WAN fabric. Virtual WAN natively provides hub-and-spoke connectivity, but it
doesn't inherently speak the specific SD-WAN protocol or have the advanced routing capabilities of 3rd party
solutions. To bridge this gap, a Network Virtual Appliance (NVA) is essential.
An NVA, deployed within the Azure Virtual WAN hub's virtual network, acts as a gateway and intelligent
routing engine. It can be a virtual instance of the SD-WAN vendor's appliance. This NVA performs several
crucial functions:
1. SD-WAN Protocol Translation: The NVA understands and participates in the 3rd party SD-WAN
protocol, allowing communication between the on-premises SD-WAN network and Azure Virtual
WAN.
2. Advanced Routing and Policy Enforcement: The NVA enforces the SD-WAN's routing policies and
traffic shaping rules within Azure, ensuring consistent network behavior across the hybrid
environment.
3. Security Integration: The NVA often provides security features like firewalls, intrusion
detection/prevention, and VPN termination, integrating these functionalities into the SD-WAN fabric.
By deploying an NVA that is compliant with the 3rd party SD-WAN solution, Azure can be seamlessly
integrated as a node within that solution. The NVA handles the routing, security, and SD-WAN protocol
translation needed for proper integration.
Other options are incorrect because:
A. Azure Virtual WAN ExpressRoute gateway: While ExpressRoute provides dedicated connectivity to Azure,
it doesn't integrate with 3rd party SD-WANs. ExpressRoute is more of a direct connection between an on-
premises environment and an Azure VNet.
C. Site-to-site gateway (VPN gateway): A VPN gateway provides basic IPsec VPN connectivity, but lacks the
features needed to integrate into an existing 3rd party SD-WAN fabric and handle SD-WAN protocols. It does
not support advanced routing policies.
D. Point-to-site gateway (User VPN gateway): User VPN gateways are for individual user access to Azure,
and not for site-to-site network integration with an SD-WAN. It will not allow your on-premises networks to
connect to Azure.
For further research:
Azure Virtual WAN Documentation: https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/virtual-wan/
Network Virtual Appliances on Azure: https://azuremarketplace.microsoft.com/en-
us/marketplace/category/networking

Question: 32 CertyIQ
You have an on-premises datacenter and an Azure subscription.
You plan to implement ExpressRoute FastPath.
You need to create an ExpressRoute gateway. The solution must minimize downtime if a single Azure datacenter
fails.
Which SKU should you use?
A.ErGw1AZ
B.High performance
C.Ultra performance
D.ErGw3AZ
E.ErGw2AZ

Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D. ErGw3AZ. Here's a detailed justification:
ExpressRoute FastPath optimizes the data path between the on-premises network and Azure virtual
networks. It bypasses the ExpressRoute gateway for direct connectivity to virtual machines within the virtual
network, improving performance. To minimize downtime during an Azure datacenter failure, zone-redundant
ExpressRoute gateways are essential. Zone redundancy ensures that the gateway is distributed across
multiple availability zones within an Azure region.
The ErGw3AZ SKU offers the highest level of availability and performance among the zone-redundant
ExpressRoute gateway SKUs. It provides zone redundancy, spreading the gateway infrastructure across
multiple availability zones within a region, thereby protecting against zonal failures. This provides better
availability than the single-instance or dual-instance non-zone-redundant gateways and the smaller ErGw1AZ
and ErGw2AZ offerings. It also scales for larger throughput and more connections compared to the ErGw1AZ
and ErGw2AZ gateways.
The other options are less suitable:
ErGw1AZ and ErGw2AZ: These are zone-redundant SKUs but offer lower performance and capacity than
ErGw3AZ. They might not be sufficient for demanding workloads or large on-premises networks, increasing
the likelihood of performance bottlenecks and potential downtime if you require scaling in response to a
failure.
High Performance and Ultra Performance: These SKUs are not zone-redundant. While they offer high
throughput, they are tied to a single Azure datacenter and will experience downtime if that datacenter fails.
ErGw3AZ: is the correct answer since it is zone-redundant and provides a high level of availablity and
capacity.
In summary, ErGw3AZ offers the best balance of high performance, scalability, and zone redundancy, which is
crucial for minimizing downtime during an Azure datacenter failure when using ExpressRoute FastPath. The
goal is to provide a resilient connection to Azure that can withstand zonal outages, and ErGw3AZ fulfills this
requirement most effectively.
Authoritative Links:
About ExpressRoute virtual network gateways
Gateway SKUs
Question: 33 CertyIQ

You have an Azure subscription that contains the resources shown in the following table.
You establish BGP peering between NVA1 and Hub1.
You need to implement transit connectivity between VNet1 and VNet3 via Hub1 by using BGP peering. The solution
must minimize costs.

What should you do? To answer, select the appropriate options in the answer area.
NOTE: Each correct selection is worth one point.
Answer:
Explanation:
1. The defaultRouteTable and associate the routes with the defaultRouteTable.
Hub-and-spoke topology typically uses a central Hub (Hub1) to connect multiple spoke VNets (VNet1, VNet2,
etc.).
In Azure Virtual WAN, routes can be propagated to connected VNets via:
A default route table (simpler and automatic)
Custom route tables (manual and more flexible)
2.User-defined routes.
User-defined routes (UDRs) allow custom control over traffic flow.
In Azure, by default, system routes handle routing, but they may not always meet specific needs.
Question: 34 CertyIQ
You have an Azure subscription that contains an ExpressRoute Standard gateway named GW1.
You need to upgrade GW1 to support ExpressRoute FastPath. The solution must minimize downtime.
Which SKU should you use?
A.Ultra performance
B.ErGw3AZ
C.ErGw2AZ
D.High performance

Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A. Ultra performance. Here's a detailed justification:
The requirement is to upgrade an existing ExpressRoute Standard gateway (GW1) to support FastPath while
minimizing downtime. ExpressRoute FastPath improves data plane performance by bypassing the
ExpressRoute gateway for certain traffic, routing directly to virtual machines in Azure VNets. This
significantly reduces latency.
To enable FastPath, the ExpressRoute gateway SKU must be compatible. Not all gateway SKUs support
FastPath. The Ultra Performance gateway SKU is the highest performing ExpressRoute gateway SKU and
does support FastPath. Choosing this SKU ensures FastPath functionality is available.
While ErGw3AZ and ErGw2AZ are zone-redundant gateway SKUs, they are designed for availability and don't
necessarily provide the highest performance needed to fully benefit from FastPath's reduced latency
capabilities. The High Performance SKU, while better than Standard, is also not optimal for maximizing
FastPath benefits compared to Ultra Performance.
The key to minimizing downtime during the upgrade is the upgrade process itself. Azure allows in-place SKU
upgrades for ExpressRoute gateways. When upgrading, Azure will first provision the new gateway instance
with the new SKU. Once the new instance is ready, traffic is seamlessly migrated from the old gateway to the
new one. Because the Ultra Performance SKU is readily available for upgrade, this process keeps downtime
minimal. Also, in general, upgrades between gateway SKUs of different performance tiers are designed to be
as non-disruptive as possible. The Ultra Performance SKU is the best choice to support FastPath and minimize
impact.
Therefore, selecting the Ultra Performance SKU provides the necessary support for ExpressRoute FastPath
while facilitating a relatively quick and minimally disruptive upgrade, satisfying the stated requirements.
For further research, consider these authoritative links:
About ExpressRoute virtual network gateways: https://learn.microsoft.com/en-
us/azure/expressroute/expressroute-about-virtual-network-gateways
About ExpressRoute FastPath: https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/expressroute/expressroute-about-
fastpath
ExpressRoute Gateway SKUs: https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/expressroute/expressroute-virtual-
network-gateways#gateway-skus
Question: 35 CertyIQ
HOTSPOT
-
Your on-premises network uses an IP address range of 10.1.0.0 to 10.1.255.255.
You plan to deploy a new Azure virtual network solution that will include the following elements:
•A virtual network named VNet1
•A Site-to-Site (S2S) VPN connection between VNet1 and the on-premises network
•GatewaySubnet in VNet1, which will be used as a route-based virtual network gateway
You need to recommend which subnet masks to assign to VNet1 and GatewaySubnet. The solution must meet the
following requirements:
•Maximize the number of available IP addresses on VNet1.
•Minimize the number of available IP addresses on GatewaySubnet.
Which address spaces should you assign to VNet1 and GatewaySubnet? To answer, select the appropriate options
in the answer area.
NOTE: Each correct selection is worth one point.

Answer:
Explanation:
1. VNet Address Space: 10.0.0.0/16

A Virtual Network (VNet) is a fundamental networking component in Azure that defines the IP address range
for connected resources.
The choice of 10.0.0.0/16 means:
It provides 65,536 IP addresses (from 10.0.0.0 to 10.0.255.255).
This allows for a large network with multiple subnets.
It is a good choice for scalable deployments where multiple subnets and services will be hosted.
2. Gateway Subnet: 10.0.0.0/27.
A Gateway Subnet is required for an Azure VPN Gateway or ExpressRoute Gateway to function.
The choice of 10.0.0.0/27 means:
32 IP addresses (from 10.0.0.0 to 10.0.0.31).
This is a recommended size for most deployments.
It allows for future scaling of gateway instances and services like BGP peering.

Question: 37 CertyIQ
HOTSPOT
-
You have an Azure subscription that contains a virtual network named VNet1.
You need to implement hybrid connectivity between an on-premises network and VNet1. The solution must meet
the following requirements:
•All cross-premises network traffic must traverse an ExpressRoute circuit.
•All cross-premises network traffic must be encrypted by using a Site-to-Site (S2S) VPN.
What should you include in the solution? To answer, select the appropriate options in the answer area.
NOTE: Each correct selection is worth one point.
Answer:
Explanation:
1. Type of ExpressRoute Peering: Private.

Azure ExpressRoute supports multiple peering types:
Microsoft Peering – For SaaS services like Microsoft 365.
Private Peering – For connecting to Azure virtual networks (VNets), extending on-premises networks.
"Private" Peering is the correct choice because:
It enables direct, private connectivity to Azure VNets.
It is required when using ExpressRoute for hybrid cloud solutions.
It is necessary for ExpressRoute and VPN coexistence.
2. Prefix Advertisement Strategy: A more specific prefix for the VPN BGP session than the ExpressRoute
BGP session.
In hybrid networking, ExpressRoute and VPN often coexist as primary and backup connections.
BGP (Border Gateway Protocol) is used to exchange routing information between Azure and on-premises.
Prefix Advertisement Strategy:
More specific prefixes for VPN ensure that traffic prefers the VPN connection.
Less specific prefixes for ExpressRoute allow it to serve as a backup or default path.
This setup ensures that VPN takes priority when necessary, avoiding asymmetric routing issues.

Question: 40 CertyIQ
DRAG DROP
-
You have 100 on-premises servers with IP addresses from the 10.0.0.0/24 IP address space.
You have an Azure subscription that contains a virtual network named VNet1, an Azure VPN gateway named VGW1,
and 100 virtual machines. VNet1 has an IP address space of 10.0.0.0/22. VGW1 uses the VpnGw1 SKU.
You need to ensure that the Azure virtual machines and the on-premises servers can communicate by using VGW1.
The solution must minimize administrative effort.
Which four actions should you perform in sequence? To answer, move the appropriate actions from the list of
actions to the answer area and arrange them in the correct order.
Answer: 2>6>4>3
Explanation:
Resize VGW1 .
Virtual Network Gateway (VGW1) may need resizing for higher throughput, additional connections, or different
SKU support.
Resizing is often the first step before configuring further network connections.

On VGW1, create a local gateway .
A Local Network Gateway (LNG) is needed when setting up a VPN connection to on-premises networks.
The local gateway represents the on-premises endpoint (e.g., a VPN device or firewall).
This step ensures Azure knows where to send traffic for hybrid connectivity.
On VGW1, add a connection .
Once the Local Network Gateway (LNG) exists, a connection between VGW1 and LNG must be established.
This step configures Site-to-Site (S2S) VPN or ExpressRoute.
Configure an Azure extended network.
The Azure Extended Network feature helps extend on-premises subnets into Azure VNets, allowing seamless
communication between Azure and on-premises workloads.
This is an optional but useful step for hybrid networking.
Question: 41 CertyIQ
DRAG DROP
-
You have a computer named CLIENT1 that runs Windows 11 and has the Azure VPN Client installed.
You have an Azure virtual network gateway named VPNGW1.
You need to ensure that you can connect CLIENT1 to VPNGW1. The solution must support Microsoft Entra
authentication.
Which four actions should you perform in sequence? To answer, move the appropriate actions from the list of
actions to the answer are and arrange them in the correct order.

Answer:

Explanation:
Step 1: Authorize the Azure VPN Application
Before configuring the VPN client, Azure VPN must be authorized in the Azure Active Directory.
This is required for authentication, especially if Azure AD authentication is used.
Action: In the Azure portal, go to Enterprise applications → Register the Azure VPN Client.
Step 2: Configure the Tunnel Type and Authentication for VPN Gateway (VPNGW1)
The Azure VPN Gateway (VPNGW1) must be set up with the correct:
Tunnel type (IKEv2, OpenVPN, or SSTP).
Authentication method (Certificate, RADIUS, or Azure AD).
Action: Navigate to Azure VPN Gateway settings, configure the tunnel and authentication, and save changes.
Step 3: Download the Azure VPN Client Configuration Package
The VPN client needs a configuration file to establish a connection.
The Azure VPN Client profile configuration package contains necessary settings like:
VPN server address

Authentication settings
Tunnel configurations
Action: In the Azure portal, go to VPN Gateway → Point-to-Site configuration → Download the configuration
package.
Step 4: Import the Configuration File on CLIENT1
Once the VPN configuration package is downloaded, the .xml file (e.g., Azurevpnconfig.xml) must be imported
into the VPN client.
This ensures the client has the correct settings to establish a connection.
Action: Open the Azure VPN Client on CLIENT1, import the Azurevpnconfig.xml file, and connect to the VPN.

Azure Firewall instance named FW1. VNet1 peers with VNet2.
The on-premises network is connected to VNet1 by using ExpressRoute. The on-premises network is inaccessible
from VNet2.
You need to ensure that virtual machines connected to VNet2 use Server1 to perform name resolution. The solution
must minimize administrative effort.
What should you do? To answer, select the appropriate options in the answer area.
NOTE: Each correct answer is worth one point.
Answer:
Explanation:

Why Other Options Are Incorrect:
On VNet1:
A DNAT rule for FW1: DNAT is for forwarding specific traffic to internal resources. It does not apply to DNS
resolution.
A DNS proxy for FW1: This is likely a typo or misunderstood term. The DNS proxy feature is enabled
automatically when Azure Firewall is used for DNS forwarding with custom DNS settings, so there's no
separate configuration for "DNS proxy."
On VNet2:
The IP address of Server1: VNet2 cannot directly access Server1 because there is no direct connectivity
between VNet2 and the on-premises network.
The public IP address of FW1: Public IPs are for external traffic and are irrelevant for internal DNS resolution.

Question: 43 CertyIQ
HOTSPOT
-
You create an ExpressRoute circuit named ERC1 that is enabled by your connectivity provider.
You need to ensure that the routes for Azure Backup and Azure Cosmos DB are advertised to the on-premises
network via ECR1.
The solution must minimize administrative effort.
What should you do? To answer, select the appropriate options in the answer area.
NOTE: Each correct selection is worth one point.
Answer:
Box1 -> Microsoft peering || Box 2 -> A route filter and two filter rules
Explanation:
You cannot use a single route filter with a single filter rule if you need access to multiple Azure services like
Azure Backup and Azure Cosmos DB. Each Azure Service Has a Unique BGP Community Value. A single filter
rule in a route filter can only specify one BGP community value. Therefore, a single rule cannot encompass
multiple services.
https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/expressroute/how-to-routefilter-portal

Why Other Options Are Incorrect:
On the ExpressRoute circuit:
Azure Private Peering: This is used for private Azure resources such as VNets and is not relevant for public
services like Azure Backup or Cosmos DB.
Associate the ExpressRoute circuit with:
A route filter and a single filter rule: This would only allow routes for one service (e.g., Azure Backup or
Cosmos DB) to be advertised, which does not meet the requirement.
Two route filters and a single filter rule: Using two route filters increases administrative overhead
unnecessarily and is not required for this scenario.

intermediary device such as a VPN Gateway, Virtual Appliance, or Network Virtual Appliance (NVA).

Other options like Application Gateway and Load Balancer are more for traffic distribution rather than secure
remote access.

connection.

Question: 46 CertyIQ
You have an on-premises network.
You have an Azure subscription that contains a virtual network.
You have an ExpressRoute service provider.
You plan to connect the Azure virtual network and the on-premises network by using an ExpressRoute circuit.
You create a new ExpressRoute circuit.
You need to provision the new circuit.
Which information should you provide to the service provider?
A.the IKEv2 shared key
B.the certificate
C.the public IP address
D.the service key
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D. the service key.
The service key, also known as the provisioning key, is a unique identifier that Microsoft Azure generates for
each ExpressRoute circuit. This key is essential for establishing the connection between your Azure
subscription and the ExpressRoute service provider. The service provider uses this key to validate the circuit
and associate it with your Azure subscription, ensuring that the ExpressRoute connection is properly
provisioned and billed to the correct account. It is the linchpin in connecting your resources.
The IKEv2 shared key (A) is relevant for VPN connections, not ExpressRoute. Certificates (B) can be used for
authentication in various scenarios, but not for the initial provisioning of an ExpressRoute circuit. Public IP
addresses (C) are necessary for resources that need to be accessed from the internet but are not directly
related to the provisioning of the ExpressRoute circuit itself. It's used later for configuring peering.
In essence, the service key is the handshake needed between Microsoft's system and your service provider.
Without it, there's no way to link your new circuit to your Azure account. Once the service provider provisions
the ExpressRoute circuit using the service key, you can then configure peering and routing between your on-

premises network and Azure.
Further reading:
ExpressRoute Documentation: https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/expressroute/expressroute-
introduction
ExpressRoute Circuits and Peering: https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/expressroute/expressroute-
circuit-peerings
Question: 47 CertyIQ
You have an on-premises server named Server1 that runs Windows Server.
You have an Azure subscription that contains a virtual network named VNet1.
You plan to connect Server1 to VNet1 by using Azure Network Adapter.
You need to minimize how long it takes to deploy the adapter to Server1.
What should you create first?
A.a route server
B.an Azure Bastion host
C.a private endpoint
D.an Azure VPN gateway
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D. an Azure VPN gateway. Here's a detailed justification:
The goal is to quickly connect an on-premises server (Server1) to an Azure virtual network (VNet1) using Azure
Network Adapter. Azure Network Adapter is a feature that facilitates point-to-site VPN connections from a
Windows Server directly to an Azure VNet. For this connection to function correctly, an Azure VPN gateway
must be created within the VNet. The Azure VPN gateway serves as the endpoint for the VPN connection
initiated from Server1.
The other options are not suitable for this scenario:
A. a route server: Azure Route Server is designed to simplify the routing configuration within an Azure virtual
network, particularly when using network virtual appliances (NVAs). It isn't a prerequisite for establishing a
basic point-to-site VPN connection.
B. an Azure Bastion host: Azure Bastion provides secure RDP/SSH access to VMs within a VNet without
exposing them to the public internet. It is not required for establishing a point-to-site VPN connection for
Azure Network Adapter.
C. a private endpoint: Azure Private Endpoint provides a private connection to Azure services from within your
VNet, preventing the need to expose the service to the public internet. It is used for securely accessing Azure
PaaS services, and not for connecting an on-premises server to an Azure VNet.
Creating the VPN gateway before deploying the Azure Network Adapter ensures that the necessary Azure-
side infrastructure is in place to immediately establish the VPN connection once the adapter is configured on
Server1. This reduces the overall time required to deploy the adapter and establish the connection. Without a
pre-existing VPN gateway, the Azure Network Adapter configuration on Server1 would be incomplete, as
there would be no endpoint to connect to.

Supporting Links:
About Azure VPN Gateway: https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/vpn-gateway/vpn-gateway-about
Configure a Point-to-Site VPN connection with native Azure certificate authentication:
https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/vpn-gateway/vpn-gateway-howto-point-to-site-resource-manager-
portal

Microsoft Defender External Attack Surface Management (Defender EASM): Provides an inventory of all
external-facing assets and determine which are accessible from the internet, including virtual machines. It

the subscription and resource configuration, such as virtual machines.

Question: 49 CertyIQ
You have an instance of Azure Web Application Firewall (WAF) on Azure Front Door.
You plan to create a WAF rule that will block high rates of requests from a single IP address.
You need to query Log Analytics to identify the optimal threshold for the rule.
Which table should you query in Log Analytics?
A.AZFWThreatIntel
B.AzureDiagnostics
C.SecurityDetection
D.AGWFirewallLogs
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B. AzureDiagnostics. Here's a detailed justification:
To identify the optimal threshold for blocking high rates of requests from a single IP address using an Azure
Web Application Firewall (WAF) on Azure Front Door, you need to analyze logs that capture the request
patterns and volume originating from specific IP addresses. AzureDiagnostics is the table in Log Analytics
where diagnostic logs from Azure Front Door, including WAF logs, are stored.
These logs contain valuable information about each request, such as the source IP address, the requested
URL, timestamps, and any WAF rule matches. By querying the AzureDiagnostics table, you can aggregate and
analyze the number of requests originating from each IP address over a specific time period. This allows you
to identify the typical request rates and detect anomalies that might indicate malicious activity or excessive
traffic.
Tables such as AZFWThreatIntel, SecurityDetection, and AGWFirewallLogs are not directly relevant in this
scenario. AZFWThreatIntel relates to Azure Firewall's threat intelligence logs. SecurityDetection focuses on
broader security detections within Azure Security Center (now Microsoft Defender for Cloud).
AGWFirewallLogs pertains to Application Gateway's firewall logs, not Azure Front Door's WAF.
Therefore, querying AzureDiagnostics with appropriate Kusto Query Language (KQL) statements is the most
efficient and direct method for determining the optimal threshold for the WAF rule. You would look for
patterns showing the request counts from different IP Addresses and what would be considered abnormal.
This analysis informs the configuration of a WAF custom rule to block requests exceeding the determined
threshold, preventing potential attacks like DDoS or bot-driven traffic.
Supporting documentation:
Azure Front Door Diagnostics: https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/frontdoor/front-door-diagnostics
Azure Front Door WAF logs: https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/web-application-firewall/afdwaf-front-
door-monitor
Kusto Query Language (KQL): https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/data-explorer/kusto/query/

Question: 50 CertyIQ

-

Question: 52 CertyIQ
HOTSPOT
-
Case Study
-
This is a case study. Case studies are not timed separately. You can use as much exam time as you would like to
complete each case. However, there may be additional case studies and sections on this exam. You must manage
your time to ensure that you are able to complete all questions included on this exam in the time provided.
To answer the questions included in a case study, you will need to reference information that is provided in the
case study. Case studies might contain exhibits and other resources that provide more information about the
scenario that is described in the case study. Each question is independent of the other questions in this case study.
At the end of this case study, a review screen will appear. This screen allows you to review your answers and to
make changes before you move to the next section of the exam. After you begin a new section, you cannot return
to this section.
To start the case study
-
To display the first question in this case study, click the Next button. Use the buttons in the left pane to explore
the content of the case study before you answer the questions. Clicking these buttons displays information such
as business requirements, existing environment, and problem statements. When you are ready to answer a
question, click the Question button to return to the question.
Overview
-
Proseware, Inc. is a financial services company that has a main office in New York City and a branch office in San
Francisco.
Existing Environment. Hybrid Environment
Proseware has an on-premises Active Directory Domain Services (AD DS) forest named corp.proseware.com that
syncs with a Microsoft Entra tenant named proseware.com.
Proseware has an Azure subscription that is linked to proseware.com.

Proseware has an internal certification authority (CA).
Existing Environment. Network Infrastructure
The offices contain the resources shown in the following table.
NYCNet connects to Azure by using an ExpressRoute circuit.
SFONet connects to Azure by using a Site-to-Site (S2S) VPN.
Existing Environment. Azure Resources
The Azure subscription contains the virtual networks and subnets shown in the following table.
The subscription contains four virtual machines named VM1, VM2, VM3, and VM4. VM1 and VM2 host an app named
App1.
VM3 and VM4 host a web app named App2 that is accessed by using a FQDN of app2.proseware.com. Users
access app2.proseware.com by using HTTP or HTTPS.
VM1, VM2, and VM4 are connected to SpokeVNet.
The subscription contains Application Gateway resources shown in the following table.

The subscription contains an Azure Front Door Standard profile named FD1. FD1 contains a single origin group that
targets APPGW1 by using the default endpoint name.
HubVNet connects to NYCNet by using an ExpressRoute gateway named ERGW1.
Planned Changes and Requirements. Planned Changes
Proseware plans to implement the following changes:
•Deploy an Azure Private DNS Resolver named PRDNS1 to HubVNet and link PRDNS1 to SpokeVNet.
•Create a DNS forwarding ruleset named DNSRS1 and associate DNSRS1 with PRDNS1.
•Deploy Azure Virtual Network Manager and implement the following rules:
- Allow inbound connections on TCP port 3389 from the on-premises networks to SUBNET-JUMPHOSTS.
- Block inbound connections on TCP port 80 from the internet to SpokeVNet.
•Ensure that Azure Virtual Network Manager rules take precedence over conflicting NSG rules.
•Deploy two network virtual appliances (NVAs) named NVA1 and NVA2 to HubVNet.
•Deploy a gateway load balancer named LBGW1 to HubVNet.
•Configure LBGW1 to inspect traffic on TCP ports 443, 1433, and 1434 from LBS1 by using NVA1 and NVA2.
•Ensure that all the traffic to App2 is processed by using FD1.
Planned Changes and Requirements. Connectivity requirements
Proseware identifies the following connectivity requirements:
•Minimize the complexity of the Azure Virtual Network Manager deployment.
•Route traffic between NYCNet and SFONet via the ExpressRoute circuit and the S2S VPN.
•Ensure that remote users on Windows 11 devices can connect to HubVNet by using a Point-to-Site (P2S) VPN and
their proseware.com credentials.
Planned Changes and Requirements. Security requirements
Proseware identifies the following security requirements:
•Whenever possible, use the internal CA.
•Ensure that all connections routed via APPGW1 use end-to-end encryption.
•Ensure that user connections to Azure-hosted apps use end-to-end encryption.
•Ensure that all inbound internet traffic to app2.proseware.com is routed via FD1.
•Prevent devices that connect to NYCNet from accessing Azure services that use private endpoints.
•Enable the virtual machines that connect to HubVNet and SpokeVNet to access Azure services that use private
endpoints.
Planned Changes and Requirements. General requirements
Proseware identifies the following general requirements:
•Minimize the IP address space required to deploy platform-managed resources to the virtual networks.
•From SpokeVNet, resolve name resolution requests for the azure.proseware.com namespace and the
corp.proseware.com namespace by using PRDNS1.
•Whenever possible, minimize administrative effort.
You need to configure the P2S VPN to meet the connectivity requirements.
What should you do? To answer, select the appropriate options in the answer area.
NOTE: Each correct selection is worth one point.

Answer:
Explanation:
1. VPNGW1 Tunnel Type: OpenVPN (SSL).
VPNGW1 refers to a VPN Gateway configuration in Azure.
The user is selecting OpenVPN (SSL) as the tunnel type.
OpenVPN (SSL) is a preferred option because:
It is secure and widely supported across different platforms.
It works well behind firewalls and supports certificates for authentication.
It is often more reliable than IKEv2 or SSTP in environments with network restrictions.
2. For proseware.com: Configure an Enterprise Application.
The second selection is about configuring an enterprise application for proseware.com.

This likely refers to Azure Active Directory (Azure AD), where:
Enterprise applications are pre-integrated SaaS applications (like Microsoft 365, Salesforce, etc.) that
organizations use for single sign-on (SSO) and identity management.
Choosing "Configure an enterprise application" suggests the user is setting up SSO or integrating a third-

Question: 53 CertyIQ
You have an Azure application gateway named AppGW1 that balances requests to a web app named App1.
You need to modify the server variables in the response header of App1.
What should you configure on AppGW1?
A.URL rewrite rules
B.path-based rules
C.listeners
D.HTTP settings
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A: URL rewrite rules.
URL rewrite rules in Azure Application Gateway allow modification of HTTP request and response headers and
URLs. Specifically, to modify the server variables in the response header of App1, we need a mechanism to
intercept and alter the outgoing HTTP response. URL rewrite rules provide this capability. They can inspect
the response from the backend server (App1 in this case) and rewrite the headers before sending the response
to the client.
Path-based rules are primarily used for routing traffic to different backend pools based on the URL path in the
request, not for modifying response headers. Listeners are used to accept incoming traffic on specified ports
and protocols, and are not directly involved in modifying response headers. HTTP settings configure backend
server parameters like port, protocol, and cookie-based affinity, and are also not the correct tool for
modifying response headers.
Therefore, only URL rewrite rules provide the functionality needed to inspect and modify the server variables
in the HTTP response header of App1 as it is sent from the application gateway to the client. This makes it the
ideal solution for the stated requirement.
https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/application-gateway/rewrite-http-headers-
urlhttps://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/application-gateway/url-rewrite-overview
